{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_013f3SLZNJ1weiRaYnK5WZ2G","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: //! The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\\n2: //! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\\n3: //! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \\\"backtrace\\\" of each\\n4: //! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\\n5: //! place).\\n6: //!\\n7: //! ### External view\\n8: //!\\n9: //! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\\n10: //! few others not discussed here):\\n11: //!\\n12: //! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\\n13: //! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\\n14: //!\\n15: //! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\\n16: //! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\\n17: //! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\\n18: //! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\\n19: //! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\\n20: //! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\\n21: //! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\\n22: //! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\\n23: //! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\\n24: //!\\n25: //! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\\n26: //!   nor a failure. It\n52: /// consists of a list of obligations that must be (eventually)\n53: /// satisfied. The job is to track which are satisfied, which yielded\n54: /// errors, and which are still pending. At any point, users can call\n55: /// `try_evaluate_obligations`, and the fulfillment context will try to do\n56: /// selection, retaining only those obligations that remain\n57: /// ambiguous. The chain flows through several key components:\\n\\n1. **Obligation Forest (compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs)**: The foundational data structure that tracks outstanding obligations as a forest of trees. Each obligation can generate sub-obligations, forming a dependency graph. The ObligationForest manages the state of obligations (pending, completed, or error) and processes them recursively through process_obligations().\\n\\n2. **Fulfillment Context (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs)**: The FulfillmentContext wraps an ObligationForest and manages the trait resolution process. It maintains PendingPredicateObligations which combine a PredicateObligation with stalled type variables. The context provides register_obligation() to add new obligations and select() to process them.\\n\\n3. **Fulfill Processor (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs)**: The FulfillProcessor implements the ObligationProcessor trait and is the callback used during obligation forest processing. It bridges the obligation forest with the SelectionContext, processing each obligation through trait selection.\\n\\n4. **Selection Context (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs)**: The core selection engine that attempts to select a trait implementation for an obligation. It uses select() to find a matching implementation and returns SelectionResult which can be Ok(Some(selection)), Ok(None) for ambiguous cases, or Err for unsatisfied obligations.\\n\\n5. **Candidate Assembly (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/candidate_assembly.rs)**: The assemble_candidates() method collects all possible implementations that could satisfy a trait obligation. It considers:\\n   - Explicit impls in scope\\n   - Trait aliases\\n   - Builtin trait implementations (Sized, Copy, Clone, etc.)\\n   - Caller's where-clause bounds (param env candidates)\\n   - Auto trait implementations\\n\\n6. **Candidate Confirmation (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/confirmation.rs)**: The confirm_candidate() method validates a selected candidate by:\\n   - Unifying the candidate's trait ref with the obligation's trait ref\\n   - Collecting nested obligations from the impl\\n   - Returning nested PredicateObligations that must also be satisfied\\n   - Handling different candidate types (ImplCandidate, ParamCandidate, BuiltinCandidate, etc.)\\n\\n7. **Error Reporting (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/error_reporting/traits/mod.rs)**: When obligations cannot be fulfilled, the report_fulfillment_errors() method generates user-facing diagnostics. It:\\n   - Aggregates errors from failed obligations\\n   - Suggests potential fixes (add trait bounds, use type parameters, etc.)\\n   - Provides context about which impls were considered but rejected\\n   - Reports impl mismatch errors with detailed suggestions\\n\\nThe complete obligation chain works as follows:\\nFulfillmentContext::register_obligation() → FulfillmentContext::select() → ObligationForest::process_obligations() → FulfillProcessor::process_obligation() → SelectionContext::select() → assemble_candidates() → candidate filtering → confirm_candidate() → nested obligations → Error or Success → report_fulfillment_errors()\\n\\nWhen an obligation fails at any point (no matching impls, nested obligations fail, or type mismatch), the error flows back through the obligation tree, ultimately being reported via the error reporting system which provides helpful diagnostics to the user.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":2298,"cache_read_input_tokens":79973,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":2298},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"8fa18a5b-3cb0-4406-bcca-d2720977359d","uuid":"7aef61b7-8557-4763-94e1-e99550ad7568"}

The chain flows through several key components:\\n\\n1. **Obligation Forest (compiler/rustc_data_structures/src/obligation_forest/mod.rs)**: The foundational data structure that tracks outstanding obligations as a forest of trees. The ObligationForest manages the state of obligations (pending, completed, or error) and processes them recursively through process_obligations().\\n\\n2. **Fulfillment Context (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs)**: The FulfillmentContext wraps an ObligationForest and manages the trait resolution process. It maintains PendingPredicateObligations which combine a PredicateObligation with stalled type variables. The context provides register_obligation() to add new obligations and select() to process them.\\n\\n3. **Fulfill Processor (compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/fulfill.rs)**: The FulfillProcessor implements the ObligationProcessor trait and is the callback used during obligation forest processing.
